{{etyl|bn|en}} {{term|ঢাকি|lang=bn}}
*Bengali: {{lang|bn|গ৷নজ৷}}
{{table-add|col1=Bangladeshi|bn|আমি বাংলাদেশি|tr=ami bangladeshi}}
* Bengali: {{t|bn|আমার অনুবাদক লাগবে|tr=amar ônubadôk lagbe|sc=Beng}}
* Bengali: {{t|bn|আমি ইংরেজি|tr=āmi inrējī|sc=Beng}}
The simple present tense of &quot;to be&quot; is not typically used in Bengali. For example, there is no verb required in the sentence {{lang|bn|আমি মার্কিন}} (ami markin), which translates as &quot;I am (an) American&quot;, while it literally means &quot;I American&quot;.
      <text xml:space="preserve">{{topic cat|bn|Capital cities}}</text>

#: {{lang|bn|আমার ভাই '''আছে'''}}
#: {{lang|bn|তোমার কী ভাই '''আছে'''?}}
* As seen in the above example sentences, this word is used to express possession when used with possessives/genitives. For example {{lang|bn|[[আমার]] [[ভাই]] '''আছে'''}} (amar bhai ache) word for word means &quot;my brother there is&quot; and translates as &quot;I have a brother&quot;.
* The negative form is {{l|bn|নাই}} (nai).

* {{l|bn|আমি বুঝি না|sc=Beng|tr=ami bujhi na}}
As Bengali verbs are conjugated for person but not number, this sentence can also be translated as &quot;we don't understand&quot;. As such, use of the personal pronoun {{term|আমি|lang=bn|sc=Beng|tr=ami}} (thus {{l|bn|আমি বুঝি না|sc=Beng|tr=ami bujhi na}}) is recommended especially if there is no prior context.</text>

* {{lang|bn|ং}} = ng ({{term|অনুস্বর|tr=ônusshôr||anusvara|lang=bn}})
* {{lang|bn|ৎ}} / {{lang|bn|ত্}} = t ({{term|খণ্ড ত|lang=bn|tr=khônḑô tô||khanda ta, broken ta}})
The bishôrgo ({{lang|bn|ঃ}}) is transliterated h when pronounced as such. When it geminates the following consonant, this is represented by doubling said consonant. If the consonant is one that is represented in transliteration with two letters (such as kh or sh) only the first is doubled (kkh or ssh).
The nasal diacritic {{l|bn|ঁ|sc=Beng}} ({{term|চন্দ্রবিন্দু|lang=bn|tr=côndrôbindu}}, the [[candrabindu|candrabindu]]) is represented by a tilde diacritic:
Conjuncts are transliterated as they are pronounced. While the pronunciation of some conjuncts is evident by their components, others are pronounced quite differently than the spelling would suggest. {{lang|bn|[[ক্ষ]]}} (the conjunct of {{lang|bn|ক}} (k) and {{lang|bn|ষ}} (sh)) is pronounced kh, and thus is transliterated as such. Others include the following:
* {{lang|bn|শ}} + {{lang|bn|ল}} = {{lang|bn|[[শ্ল]]}} (slô)
* {{lang|bn|জ}} + {{lang|bn|ঞ}} = {{lang|bn|[[জ্ঞ]]}} (ggỗ)
* {{lang|bn|স}} + {{lang|bn|ব}} = {{lang|bn|[[স্ব]]}} (shô)
The pronunciations of conjuncts ending in {{lang|bn|্য}} such as {{lang|bn|ক্য}} and {{lang|bn|ধ্য}} do not reflect the presence of the {{lang|bn|য}}, but lengthen the pronunciation of the preceding consonant and therefore are transliterated by said consonant's doubling. Thus {{lang|bn|ক্য}} and {{lang|bn|ধ্য}} are transliterated kk and ddh.

      <comment>Created page with '==Bengali==  ===Alternative forms=== * {{l|bn|জানি না|sc=Beng|tr=jani na}}  ===Phrase=== {{bn-phrase|tr=ami jani na}}  # [[I don't know]]  ===See also=== * {{l|bn|আ...'</comment>
* {{l|bn|জানি না|sc=Beng|tr=jani na}}
* {{l|bn|আমি জানতে চাই|sc=Beng|tr=ami jante cai}}</text>
* {{l|bn|আমি জানি না|sc=Beng|tr=ami jani na}}
As Bengali verbs are conjugated for person but not number, this sentence can also be translated as &quot;we don't understand&quot;. As such, use of the personal pronoun {{term|আমি|lang=bn|sc=Beng|tr=ami}} (thus {{l|bn|আমি জানি না|sc=Beng|tr=ami jani na}}) is recommended especially if there is no prior context.

***** Bengali: {{l|bn|তিন|tr=tin}}
Around {{C.E.}} 674, borrowed from {{etyl|sa|zh}} {{m|sa|पालङ्क}}, {{m|sa|पालङ्क्य}}, {{m|sa|पालक्या||Indian spinach ({{taxlink|Beta bengalensis|species|noshow=1}})}}, possibly via some ancient language in modern-day Nepal. Compare modern {{etyl|ne|-}} {{m|ne|पालुङ्गो||spinach}}, {{etyl|bn|-}} {{m|bn|পালং||tr=pālaṁ|spinach (''[[Spinacia oleracea]]'')}}. Possibly the source of {{zh-l|菠菜}}.
